          Insights

link) Date.parse accepts strings that are implementation specific. This is causing incompatibilities across runtimes with new and repeat bugs filed regularly.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSuggesting: specify the \u003cem\u003eintersection\u003c/em\u003e of supported string formats, specify this as the \u003cem\u003efallback\u003c/em\u003e for Date.parse.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://github.com/mrrrgn/proposal-date-time-string-format/blob/master/data/results.csv\"\u003ehttps://github.com/mrrrgn/proposal-date-time-string-format/blob/master/data/results.csv\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDE: How much of what is currently allowed to parse is banned under this proposal?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: In general, implementations are allowed to add extensions to do something else rather than throwing whenever they want.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDE: If any impl. doesn't apply extensions to spec: what sort of strings that currently parse, would \u003cem\u003enot\u003c/em\u003e parse (by only implementing this format)?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: (what are the data in results.csv?)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: Those are data generated by a fuzzer and the columns on the right are \"yes\" or \"no\" whether the string parsed\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: The table lists which dates are accepted, but what dates do they generate? For a concrete example, line 30 is \"may,may,-000000\". It's accepted, but what date does that produce?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: This will parse as May 1, 2000. Almost all of this is crazy, hacks on hacks\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e(shock and awe)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: Web compatibility concerns?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: Working with V8 dev to add telemetry probes into V8 and SpiderMonkey. The web is fairly broken already—implementing an \u003cem\u003eintersection\u003c/em\u003e as a fallback should not break the web.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: Is the goal to find the intersection, or a refinement on the intersection?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: Refinement.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Are there places where different impl. accept a string but generate different dates?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: Possible, but haven't explored. So far have only looked for producing a NaN\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: Should that be included?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS/AWB: Yes\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: Can we replace \"yes\" and \"no\" in the table with the actual output?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: Yes\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Does the table include all \"yes\" rows (i.e. rows where the existing implementations all accept the string)?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: removed, there are millions.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEFT: Those are covered by the proposed grammar\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: In the table there's a column for whether the proposed grammar accepts the string. It's the \"parser\" column.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Row 4839 is accepted by three implementations but not the proposed grammar.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMF: There are 60 examples like that in the table.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: The grammar needs to accept more. The current grammar isn't what I want to propose in the end.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: I want to reference back to ES5 and when we added ISO dates and what our thinking at that time was. What we did in ES5, we introduced the ISO date format and we did a quick look at this sort of stuff, and decided it was such an incredible mess that maybe there's no way to fix it. Part of the thinking there was, do we fix up this thing that's here, and identify which dates we take and which we don't take, or do we leave and assume that some day in the future we'll introduce a new API that is a date parser, and that we've designed from first principles of what dates we want to parse, and we don't simply include funny weird cases that exist in implementation-defined stuff simply because it's there. Because it's a new API, we wouldn't have compatibility requirements. That's still possible--we could try to find this intersection, or we could leave it alone and find the date parser implementation that we want.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: [Agree, but Date API is generally the sort of thing that accepts junk and is expected to do the right thing]\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDE: Unfortunately, browsers don't have the luxury of doing what AWB suggests, and the demands of web compatibility mean that we have to support what other browsers support.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMPS: noting reports that a company identified some large number of bugs being date-based.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDE: We have found that at least 4 out of 10k page loads use the \"legacy date parser\" in Chrome\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eConclusion/Resolution\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch2 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e9.iii.a System.global\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-9iiia-systemglobal\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: 9.iii.a System.global\" href=\"#9iiia-systemglobal\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJordan Harband\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ca href=\"https://github.com/tc39/proposal-global\"\u003ehttps://github.com/tc39/proposal-global\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: We reached Stage 2 previously, and the remaining open question is which name should be used. window would break lots of code, since everyone assumes 'typeof window' indicates whether you're running in a main page. The remaining options are self, global, and System.global\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: there's also frames! (jokingly)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: This is about breaking libraries like lodash, as well as breaking code which runs in Node. self has for a long time indicated that your code is used on the web, but it doesn't seem like a really big hazard; not much code for that. Also, self is used to store the receiver, though you can use arrow functions for most of those use cases these days. var self = this is a frequent idiom. Ultimately, if we pick self, Node is broken.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: We (TC39) make breaking changes to Node all the time. I think \"breaking Node\" is overstating it\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: This is a very common pattern, though it sometimes dispatches on window or module.exports.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: We already have a lot of ways to refer to the global. Do we really need another one? Further (lower priority), there is a distinction between the global proxy and the global object. Setting properties on the global scope sets it on the global object, but referring to it gets the global proxy.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e(Discussion of Domenic's concerns listed here: \u003ca class=\"issue-link js-issue-link\" data-error-text=\"Failed to load title\" data-id=\"156124449\" data-permission-text=\"Title is private\" data-url=\"https://github.com/tc39/proposal-global/issues/16\" data-hovercard-type=\"issue\" data-hovercard-url=\"/tc39/proposal-global/issues/16/hovercard?comment_id=221558082\u0026amp;comment_type=issue_comment\" href=\"https://github.com/tc39/proposal-global/issues/16#issuecomment-221558082\"\u003etc39/proposal-global#16 (comment)\u003c/a\u003e )\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: How does this work across realms? The global object is a funny thing, as depending on where you evaluate it from, you may get different ones. If the global object is a proxy, is the system object also a proxy?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: The System object is very much like the Math object\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: In an environment with multiple realms, there will be multiple System objects.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: (draws diagram to explain WindowProxy)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: Is this relevant to the System.global discussion?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: I'll reiterate that this is not adding a new capability, as you can use the Function constructor; this just gives a way to do that without eval.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: Actually IE/Edge is restricted in a way that I don't understand for calling the function constructor in some ways\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: This is one case where it's been hard for me to contribute to the web side of the standards world\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBE: Ultimately this is about things like window.setTimeout (with a string so it will do eval)? Or what situations?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: Even executing a closure.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: WindowProxy is there so that, if you navigate a frame within another frame, the \"window\" object of that frame stays the same identity, so it is a \"proxy\" to an inner global object which changes on navigation. There's no way to access the inner object from within script.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: Regardless of WindowProxy, System.global returns the global object, the same one that's accessed through 'this' or whatever else.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: Yes, this is the thing in the space of globalness that's relevant.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: So we need a way to access the global 'this' value, a way that's the same across all environments. The function constructor can't be called from CSP. So we have two options--the bare 'global', or System.global. I haven't found anyone do typeof global\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBF: Browserify's wrapper uses typeof global\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: But actually everyone uses 'typeof process' together with that when detecting Node-ness.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: Two other options for names: Object.global\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: I veto that as it would violate authority separation. I want to separate authority-carrying objects from non-authority-separating objects.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: But \u003ccode\u003eObject.__proto__\u003c/code\u003e is Function, which gives you the authority to get the global object anyway.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Function and eval are evaluators; CSP gives you the option to turn off evaluators. Any other environment such as SES/frozen realms has to intervene in the evaluators in order to constrain the scope of the evaluation. In any such environment, the function constructor has to be sanitized.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Doesn't that mean that we don't currently have authority separation, and you already have to do some work for this?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: We've addressed current pain points; let's not add to the burden.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: A lot of this seems to revolve around the function constructor. Another place to hang this would be Function.global.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Let's not spend time on things that are strictly worse\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: Mark has argued that this cannot be a global variable so that it's more easily secured.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: Sounds like a good time to bring in the Realms API and the global scope contour, which introduce additional concepts that need work in the language. It's an open area for discussion, where we might want to expose the actual current realm.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: There's something special about global. There's already three ways to access this thing; adding new ways is sorta bad. We're not adding a bunch of things; this is just accessing one thing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Right now, none of the ways of accessing global are in the ECMAScript spec, and it's a beautiful thing that the boundary between the ES spec and the host corresponds very closely to user-mode computation and system mode computation. ES standardizes no way to cause effects on the outside world; the host provides bindings on the global object to cause effects on the outside world. Because the other things are put on the global, the global itself should be considered a host object that provides access to these things. Because there is no binding to the global object, nothing grants authority. There are several future proposals which do things like that.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: We don't have any of those. Global is special. There is some advantage to making the name short. Let's say it doesn't set a convention.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: This should be a built-in module\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: So far, every time this came up, we said that we don't want to block it on this; once there's a standard modules proposal, we can consider this.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: We have a strong precedent for just calling this global. I want to understand your objection, Mark. It sounds like you're saying, let's not set the precedent of exposing a power object, when it's already exposed in reality in so many ways.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Because it's not in scope in the ES spec, an environment could claim conformance to ES without exposing this.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDE: It is in the intersection of the various popular embedding environments, however.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: I went with System.global because of the nonzero compat risk of bare 'global'. However, I haven't found any concrete compat risks. The second reason is that Mark thought it would help restrict authority to put it under a namespace.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: SES already has to care about this kind of thing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: We currently have a whitelist in SES. global is not one of them.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: So if you're OK with not adding a global, you don't have to do anything to SES?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: I'm concerned about the maintenance cost and initialization time. Spec changes cause SES to trail, which users find painful.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: But sounds like SES users will be protected anyway\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: The difference between other things considered to add to System, Loader, etc and global is that they add new capabilities, whereas global does not add a new capability. It's just exposing an existing thing. Therefore it doesn't need to be added in a particular namespace, and doesn't set a precedent.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: I hope that frozen realms will be added and hide the global object.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: It sounds like the requirement that it be under a namespace is not very strong, simply a preference\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: \"simply a preference\" is too weak. The issue of distinctions and psychological burden and precedent setting are pretty important.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDT: You're talking about the burden on developers?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: I agree that they're real issues, but users already have the burden of having this reference.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Given that you expose the global object, seems like it doesn't give a new capability.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: I'll have to think about this, but I can't approve that as a sound choice at the moment.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: If Mark were to agree to Yehuda's point, if we changed the name to 'global', would anyone object to it with the name simply 'global'?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: I'd prefer 'self'\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCM: no self\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: Would prefer \u003ccode\u003eself\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: 'global' seems fine. Most people don't seem to want 'self', Domenic.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK, AK: This doesn't give any new capability\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJHD: Sounds like the next steps are for Mark to think through Yehuda's objection and see if he can support bare 'global', and for me to follow up with Mark, Dean and \u0026lt;who?\u0026gt;\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv href=\"https://github.com/jeffmo/es-class-public-fields\"\u003ehttps://github.com/jeffmo/es-class-public-fields\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: main dir=\"auto\"\u003eInitializers execute at the time of the last\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003estatic field initializers are executed as the last step of class definition evaluation, need access to the class name binding itself.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e(discussion of the scope of initializers)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: What should be available inside the initializer?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eBanning arguments, new.target (because unclear) -- these are static semantics errors when occurring literally, and \u003ccode\u003eundefined\u003c/code\u003e in direct eval\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eAllowing this and super property access\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: It would be confusing to have the old enclosing copies of new.target or arguments inside of the initializers, which run later\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: Can't you write \"arguments\" in computed properties?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: We discussed this in the context of the cross-cutting class proposal with Brian\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eYou might want this in a static property to refer to the class you just created\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: There have been issues created in the Babel tracker about the scoping of this\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: In a static method this refers to the constructor function\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eThe constructor function that the static property is defined on\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: A consistency for static initializers for the left and right hand side of initializers would be to be \"the same as in a static body\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: open q: \"Do we permit or ban new.target or arguments in the right hand side of initializers?\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: This becomes tricky because some people expect that a field referecnes ambient bindings, but it's easy to get confused if you treat the initializer as a method\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: These initializers are very shorthand for a function, which always has new.target\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: In favor of banning\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: A use case is a static method on subclasses that filters the initializers, as called from a superclass constructor. In that case, you want to call |new.target.initializerFilter()|, and so want new.target to work\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Even though you can construct models which are consistent about which is which with new.target and arguments, it's equally hard to construct one that is unambiguously clear which one you are referring to\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: This isn't a catchall; there will still be imperative cases that benefit from being written in the constructor\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: If we ban them now, we can always add them later.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: We also need to decide what to do with eval('new.target')\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Presumably if it's an early error without eval, then it will throw early during the eval as well\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e(discussion of alternatives)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Because this is a convenience tool, we can ban eval without loss of expressiveness. It's just a loss of convenience\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: On instinct, this scares me. Just because we can't come up with a use case, doesn't mean that something won't ever come up\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: How deep would the direct eval ban go? Expression, subexpressions, within arrow functions inside subexpressions, ...?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: banning direct eval is hard, because it's undecidable whether it's direct eval\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Yeah, we'd have to ban the entire class of things that could wind up being direct eval\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM; The only reason we're allowing these outside of the constructor at all, is for common well-behaved cases\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: Think of this as shorthand for function. If it was a function, all functions define new.target. When invoked you get undefined. Functions have arguments. There are no functions. If you just treat an initializer like an anonymous function, then you get exactly everything falling out\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDE: If you treat it like just a method, then you get everything you want\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: This avoids a laundry list of special cases\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eKG: What about statics? The easy corollary is that for statics, it's an anonymous static method.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: This also allows for sane semantics for \u003ccode\u003ethis\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eKG: (whiteboard)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class Base {\n  prop = new.target.filter ? new.target.filter(val) : val;\n}\n\nclass Derived extends Base {\n  static filter() {}\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eBase\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e{\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003eprop\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003enew\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003etarget\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003efilter\u003c/span\u003e ? No, we should be able to statically determine whether eval or arguments are possible.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEF: This is a simple front-end optimization.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eConsensus: Initializers run with the semantics of individual anonymous methods with no arguments being run on the class. That explains the scope of this and super property access; new.target would be undefined, and each would get a new empty arguments object.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: Do properties get created with DefinePropertyOrThrow() or Set()?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e(whiteboard)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class FooText extends TextNode {\n  textValue = \u0026quot;asdlsk\u0026quot;;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eFooText\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eextends\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eTextNode\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e{\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etextValue\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"asdlsk\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e;\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e}\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Users would likely expect to get a Set; most users don't understand setters, and would expect that setters are always called\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH, MM: Would be really surprised by a Set in this example. The intuition is for initializers to use define.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: You could phrase this either way; either it's a hazard, or it sets the expectation that users can depend on a predictable DefinePropertyOrThrow.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: The reason why Set doesn't work is that it's not extensible to const, to typed properties, all of these can only be done on DefinePropertyOrThrow\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"textValue = \u0026quot;adadad\u0026quot;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-s1\"\u003etextValue\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"adadad\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e^^^ Authors don't immediately recognize that the difference between Set() and DefinePropertyOrThrow()\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Can't use Set() to define const or typed properties. People are very split on this. So as an argument for which is more intuitive, that's a wishy argument. We should go based on what is more useful.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: If you define a method named textValue, you can't\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBE: = looks like Set\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: So we should use colon\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Colon is reserved for type annotations\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBE/WH: the only robust semantics is DefinePropertyOrThrow()\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Only DefinePropertyOrThrow will work across future extensions, for const properties and typed properties\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eevaluate the type, around time of initializer, can't create it and later change type, so it MUST be created with DefinePropertyOrThrow()\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: How is this conflated?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: The idea that an initializer does a Set(), but a const does a DefinePropertyOrThrow() is just (confusing?)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: We already have in ES6 practice for how to initialize objects imperatively, with \u003ccode\u003ethis.textValue = \"asdf\"\u003c/code\u003e inside the constructor. That's imperative, that does a Set(), it has all the properties that Yehuda is advocating. Any proposal that adds new syntax should, to justify the cost of the new syntax, have less overlap with something you can easily say already.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"this.textValue = \u0026quot;...\u0026quot;;\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-smi\"\u003ethis\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etextValue\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003e=\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-s\"\u003e\"...\"\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e;\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e...is a Set()\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: This is shocking. That means that you are saying we shouldn't have symmetry\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: I value symmetry, but I don't see a symmetry argument. Writing object literals has the same problem.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: That's different because object literals don't have superclasses. People don't use \u003ccode\u003e__proto__\u003c/code\u003e: very much\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBE: What's the robust, future-proof semantics? The primary use case is turning an existing property into a setter or getter, to shadow something else or make something lazy. If that's the upgrade path, then this will break.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: That's a good point; people do deprecations by adding setters or getters, and that would fail because it would just shadow\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: If the semantics of this is Set, I would ask, what is the added value of the proposal as a whole such that the proposal pulls its weight. You could get these semantics just by writing the right lines in the constructor.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDE: Good from an optimizability standpoint. We've been encouraging people to be explicit about properties on \u003ccode\u003ethis\u003c/code\u003e by adding them all in the constructor, assigning \u003ccode\u003eundefined\u003c/code\u003e if necessary. This is a nice syntax for that.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Using Set() is dangerous, if derived class has foo, exposes you to a super class that didn't have accessor foo, which is later added.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Lots of classes which are designed to be subclassed assume that they can intercept Set()s\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDT: Initialization in C#, Java, etc is explicitly setting up the world and invariants aren't there\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDD: For us it's different, because super has already returned, etc\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDT: Using DefinePropertyOrThrow is good because it'll give us that capability from other languages, where you add the properties without invoking setters.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: In the current proposal (with Set), it's the same as doing the code in the constructor, so the constrained DSL is nice because it is not so order-dependent, right?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: Sounds like we won't resolve the issue in this meeting; I'll work with some people offline to come to more of a conclusion on this.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: The last open question: For fields that do not have an initializer, these implicitly initialize to undefined, not copying this.x = this.x as previously. I went back and forth on this; one of the reasons I was against this is that I was concerned about shadowing the same-named property on the parent class. But what convinced me is that, presumably, if you put that declaration there without an initializer, you would intend to initialize it later at some point, in which case you would be shadowing the parent property anyway. So the expectation is that, when you put the field there, you will be shadowing the field above it. So the initialization happening in order makes sense.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"highlight highlight-source-js notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" dir=\"auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"class FooText extends TextNode {\n  textValue; // textValue = undefined;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eclass\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eFooText\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-k\"\u003eextends\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-v\"\u003eTextNode\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e{\u003c/span\u003e\n  \u003cspan class=\"pl-c1\"\u003etextValue\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e;\u003c/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\"pl-c\"\u003e// textValue = undefined;\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cspan class=\"pl-kos\"\u003e}\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH, AWB: Good.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: In lexical scoping, we decided that the same name in the same scope would always refer to the same binding. No user complaints.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Should the properties be defined as configurable or non-configurable?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eJM: Currently it creates a non-configurable property with DefinePropertyOrThrow\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: Seems strange why we would do it differently from methods\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: I strongly prefer non-configurable. We already have an imperative syntax for imperative initialization, properties that are configurable and disappear. The time-dependent nature of configurable properties don't give you as many guarantees. Non-configurable properties let you minimize gratuitious differences with private state and get static analyzability and static shape. The behavior of private fields is more like a non-configurable property than anything else.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: I support your position, but in addition: one of the advantages of this new syntax, is that it allows to declaratively define the shape of the object.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eValue in readability\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eMake non-configurable is a powerful value\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: what happens when a super class has already defined one of these? I don't think we should advance either on their own to stage 3.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"markdown-heading\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e\u003ch4 tabindex=\"-1\" class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003eConclusion/Resolution\u003c/h4\u003e\u003ca id=\"user-content-conclusionresolution-8\" class=\"anchor\" aria-label=\"Permalink: Conclusion/Resolution\" href=\"#conclusionresolution-8\"\u003e\u003csvg class=\"octicon octicon-link\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" version=\"1.1\" width=\"16\" height=\"16\" aria-hidden=\"true\"\u003e\u003cpath d=\"m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cul dir=\"auto\"\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eStage 2 acceptance\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli\u003eInitializers run with the semantics of individual anonymous methods with no arguments being run on the class. class=\"heading-element\" dir=\"auto\"\u003e10.iii.c \u003ca href=\"https://github.com/benjamn/reify/blob/master/PROPOSAL.md\"\u003eNested import declaration\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\u003ca 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z\"\u003e\u003c/path\u003e\u003c/svg\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBen Newman\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Potentially relaxing restriction that \u003ccode\u003eimport\u003c/code\u003e can only appear at the top level.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: proposal would allow \u003ccode\u003eimport\u003c/code\u003es that are nestable; hoisted (declarative over imperative); lexically scoped; sync eval'd; back compat.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: We have been shipping this to the Meteor community in a transpiler context. The semantics are more subtle than you would expect to allow, due to the subtleties of modules. They are synchronous (hoisted to the top of the scope) and backwards compatible.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: [clarifying that bindings are immutable on the import side]\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: [clarifying that currently proposal is transpiled to commonJS require]\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e... discussion about the spec; request to skip the spec discussion at this stage ...\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: How about we consider these to be ordinary lexically scoped variables?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: If I sit inside a loop, importing a module mutiple times, will I get the same module namespace object?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Yes. In subsequent iterations, it doesn't get imported again\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Is the module specifier still restricted to only being a string literal?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Yes.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: In this proposal, no matter what, all imports will be loaded beforehand. It's only that evaluation will be deferred until it reaches that point in the code.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: Do you hoist evaluation as well as instantiation? - I would expect hoisting, for consistency with top-level imports\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: the ability to have nested imports gives you a tool to control relative execution of import declarations to other statements\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: Yes, that's the Optimistic Imports example from the proposal.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: DH's point is important. If you want predictability, you do not want interleaving.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Modules get all loaded before the program starts. Their instantiations are done as their blocks are encountered in the program.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eWH: So then what happens if a module is missing when being loaded? How do Optimistic Imports work?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: necessarily an error if it fails to load.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: ... talking about a use case for cross-env code with conditional imports ... if it turns out that the fetching of the module source fails, it is entirely conceivable that the dev knows this was a possibility and that that import is inside a conditional block that prevents it from evaluating - so I think it's less fatal for the fetch to fail.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: an important use case for this is \"if I'm in env X, import stuff for env X\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: proposal: we unconditionally do all the fetches, but if any fail, we don't actually fail - just hang onto the error for later. and only if control flow reaches the point where it's needed, does it end up being an error. iow, if you only have conditional imports, failures will not create a compile-time error, and only create a runtime error when the module is needed and missing.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: consistent with the current spec.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: changing what used to be early errors into not-early errors.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: I mean consistent in that it treats each block as if it's its own module.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: ?? conditional importing means the dev knows it's benign if it's missing, and can work around that.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: ... explaining \"isolated scopes\" example ... ability to reuse identifiers in the same file, but in separate scopes. With top-level, you need slight identifier variations.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: also refactoring hazard - if the imports are in the describe, it's easier to split up large files without breaking things.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: in top-level model you still have to do all the same fetching\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCP: at what point in this program is the error triggered? we intentionally chose declarative import evaluation as well as initialization/loading.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: the specific \"it\" test in my example will fail if the import nested inside it fails to load.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: it should fail every time its import is attempted\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: it should be possible via the registry to clear things out and make it possible to retry, but only in a staged way - ie, you have to kick off an evaluation, not in the middle of a module.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBF: in node, if it evaluates, it's put into the cache; if it fails to evaluate, it's not put into the cache.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e... discussion about entire dep graph being resolved before any evaluation ...\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDT: ... general argument that nested imports would have to be VERY compelling to make it worth it ...\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB: what about imperatively using a dynamic import API?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: loader API does not let you statically express dependencies, so we talked about a syntax that allows dynamic async importing\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e... more discussion ?? ...\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: inherent conflict with top-level await\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: I think the dynamic syntax you're proposing is essential for top-level await. what would happens with current \u003ccode\u003eimport\u003c/code\u003e if you pull in a module using top-level \u003ccode\u003eawait\u003c/code\u003e?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCP: top-level \u003ccode\u003eimport\u003c/code\u003e would handle it\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: essentially forks the world - ie, \"modules that can use top-level await\" and \"modules that can't\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: still some motivating examples worth talking about\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBF: a point: top-level await is going to pretty much wreck node's sync loading anyways\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: if top-level await turns out to be infeasible, then the conflict here is moot, but still worth talking about\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: my concern is that it makes loading unconditional + evaluating conditional, and i think conditional loading is important too\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: skipping over \"lazy eval\" claim. will note that in node, which has sync i/o, pushing requires into functions has helped startup perf (likely from deferring the i/o)\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: depends on the complexity of the file you're importing\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSM: biggest perf problem at FB is parsing and initialization. we load everything and only evaluate the things we need. we can't switch to modules without lazy eval + lazy loading.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: i think it will not interfere with lazy loading.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: if you treat all module identifiers the same, then you don't have to parse the whole file, you just have to tokenize it and look for \"import\" tokens.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eEF: i think you grossly underestimate the costs involved.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003e... discussion about tokenizing vs parsing; costs thereof; etc ...\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: in my naive understanding of tokenizing and parsing, you could tokenize, iterate, locate \u003ccode\u003eimport\u003c/code\u003e, locate the possible path - then optimistically parse that path whether it's a module or not.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: unless you're talking about throwing away all module early errors, you need to know the exports, so you still have to parse. your approach only would allow easier fetching.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: if i'm wrong about the tokenizing trick, it still doesn't matter where the import declarations are\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: i think the point is that if it turns out that conditional import ...\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSM: what matters is \"do you do the fetch if there's a syntax error\"\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCP: Do we need to have a user make a change to allow for this tokenizing optimization?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: The optimization is orthogonal\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: He means deferring evaluation\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: That seems unsafe to me.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Colocating imports and code should be good long-term for code hygiene because it should keep the things together and help you as you move the code around. And of course you can keep putting them all at the top level if you want.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Further justification: Put an import in a try/catch block  in case you have fallback behavior.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eSP: But what if it's not the first time? This scares me. You don't get the chance to execute your fallback behavior.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Maybe you should remember the throw and rethrow if it failed.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eCP: You were saying that it should go to the top\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: To the top of the block. It will still throw from within the try block.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: To me, this looks like a nested module. It seems like it would be a module in the tree which fails.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Another benefit is dead code elimination--you can avoid running the code by importing only when needed, and this then doesn't run the top-level statements.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: Dead code elimination will be approximate in JavaScript. It couldn't be done by implementations, but could be done by preprocessors which are OK with changing semantics.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eMM: Is it valid to eliminate the fetch?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Technically these change semantics, but may be OK for the application.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBF: Module resolution may not include fetch; for Node, things will be pre-populated\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eYK: We did a lot to support the web's asynchronous fetching.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Yes, we needed to support browsers. Nested import declarations seem problematic mostly because of the browser and asynchronous fetch.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: I have a grammar in the proposal. Import is not allowed in non-modules. There is a PR, I invite people to participate there. Nested imports from scripts are prohibited with static semantics.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: We have settled on declarative imports, hoisting them. But nested imports give you a tool for doing imperative imports, though no deferred fetching and specifiers are literal\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: Stage 1?\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: Suggested area of exploration: await import\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cdiv class=\"snippet-clipboard-content notranslate position-relative overflow-auto\" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content=\"async fn() {\n    await import {x} from m;\n}\"\u003e\u003cpre class=\"notranslate\"\u003e\u003ccode\u003easync fn() {\n    await import {x} from m;\n}\n\u003c/code\u003e\u003c/pre\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAWB, YK: We should merge this group with the loader group to come back in a few months.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eAK: I'm surprised you're not upset about it being a promise.\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eDH: But the Promise is not reified\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp dir=\"auto\"\u003eBN: I would prefer synchronous semantics, if possible, but we could live with this. July 27, 2016 Meeting Notes","-----","","Brian Terlson (BT), Michael Ficarra (MF), Jordan Harband (JHD), Waldemar Horwat (WH), Tim Disney (TD), Michael Saboff (MLS), Chip Morningstar (CM), Daniel Ehrenberg (DE), Leo Balter (LEO), Yehuda Katz (YK), Jafar Husain (JH), István Sebestyén (IS), John Neumann (JN), Domenic Denicola (DD), Rick Waldron (RW), Stefan Penner (SP), Jonathan Sampson (JSN), Caridy Patiño (CP), Sam Tobin-Hochstadt (STH), John Buchanan (JB), Kevin Gibbons (KG), Lars Hansen (LHN), Peter Jensen (PJ), Tom Care (TC), Dave Herman (DH), Bradley Farias (BFS), Kris Gray (KGY), Adam Klein (AK), Dean Tribble (DT), Eric Faust (EFT), Jeff Morrison (JM), Sebastian Markbåge (SM), Saam Barati (SBI), Kris Gray (KGY), John-David Dalton (JDD), Ben Newman (BN), Morgan Phillips (MPS), Shu-yu Guo (SYG), Paul Leathers (PL), Ben Smith (BS), Zibi Braniecki (ZB)","","-----","","## 9.i.g Date.parse fallback semantics","","Morgan Phillips","","https://github.com/mrrrgn/proposal-date-time-string-format","","","MPS: (see link) Date.parse accepts strings that are implementation specific. This is causing incompatibilities across runtimes with new and repeat bugs filed regularly.","","Suggesting: specify the _intersection_ of supported string formats, specify this as the _fallback_ for Date.parse.","","https://github.com/mrrrgn/proposal-date-time-string-format/blob/master/data/results.csv","","DE: How much of what is currently allowed to parse is banned under this proposal?","","AWB: In general, implementations are allowed to add extensions to do something else rather than throwing whenever they want.","","DE: If any impl. doesn't apply extensions to spec: what sort of strings that currently parse, would _not_ parse (by only implementing this format)?","","WH: (what are the data in results.csv?)","","MPS: Those are data generated by a fuzzer and the columns on the right are \"yes\" or \"no\" whether the string parsed","","WH: The table lists which dates are accepted, but what dates do they generate? For a concrete example, line 30 is \"may,may,-000000\". It's accepted, but what date does that produce?","","MPS: This will parse as May 1, 2000. Almost all of this is crazy, hacks on hacks","","(shock and awe)","","SP: Web compatibility concerns?","","MPS: Working with V8 dev to add telemetry probes into V8 and SpiderMonkey. The web is fairly broken already—implementing an _intersection_ as a fallback should not break the web.","","SP: Is the goal to find the intersection, or a refinement on the intersection?","","MPS: Refinement.","","WH: Are there places where different impl. accept a string but generate different dates?","","MPS: Possible, but haven't explored. So far have only looked for producing a NaN","","SP: Should that be included?","","MPS/AWB: Yes","","AWB: Can we replace \"yes\" and \"no\" in the table with the actual output?","","MPS: Yes","","WH: Does the table include all \"yes\" rows (i.e. rows where the existing implementations all accept the string)?","","MPS: removed, there are millions.","","EFT: Those are covered by the proposed grammar","","MPS: In the table there's a column for whether the proposed grammar accepts the string. It's the \"parser\" column.","","WH: Row 4839 is accepted by three implementations but not the proposed grammar.","","MF: There are 60 examples like that in the table.","","MPS: The grammar needs to accept more. The current grammar isn't what I want to propose in the end.","","AWB: I want to reference back to ES5 and when we added ISO dates and what our thinking at that time was. What we did in ES5, we introduced the ISO date format and we did a quick look at this sort of stuff, and decided it was such an incredible mess that maybe there's no way to fix it. Part of the thinking there was, do we fix up this thing that's here, and identify which dates we take and which we don't take, or do we leave and assume that some day in the future we'll introduce a new API that is a date parser, and that we've designed from first principles of what dates we want to parse, and we don't simply include funny weird cases that exist in implementation-defined stuff simply because it's there. Because it's a new API, we wouldn't have compatibility requirements. That's still possible--we could try to find this intersection, or we could leave it alone and find the date parser implementation that we want.","","","YK: [Agree, but Date API is generally the sort of thing that accepts junk and is expected to do the right thing]","","DE: Unfortunately, browsers don't have the luxury of doing what AWB suggests, and the demands of web compatibility mean that we have to support what other browsers support.","","MPS: noting reports that a company identified some large number of bugs being date-based.","","DE: We have found that at least 4 out of 10k page loads use the \"legacy date parser\" in Chrome","","","#### Conclusion/Resolution","","- Stage 1 acceptance","","","## 9.iii.a System.global","","Jordan Harband","","https://github.com/tc39/proposal-global","","JHD: We reached Stage 2 previously, and the remaining open question is which name should be used. window would break lots of code, since everyone assumes 'typeof window' indicates whether you're running in a main page. The remaining options are self, global, and System.global","","DD: there's also frames! (jokingly)","","JHD: This is about breaking libraries like lodash, as well as breaking code which runs in Node. self has for a long time indicated that your code is used on the web, but it doesn't seem like a really big hazard; not much code for that. Also, self is used to store the receiver, though you can use arrow functions for most of those use cases these days. var self = this is a frequent idiom. Ultimately, if we pick self, Node is broken.","","DD: We (TC39) make breaking changes to Node all the time. I think \"breaking Node\" is overstating it","","JHD: This is a very common pattern, though it sometimes dispatches on window or module.exports.","","DD: We already have a lot of ways to refer to the global. Do we really need another one? Further (lower priority), there is a distinction between the global proxy and the global object. Setting properties on the global scope sets it on the global object, but referring to it gets the global proxy.","","(Discussion of Domenic's concerns listed here: https://github.com/tc39/proposal-global/issues/16#issuecomment-221558082 )","","WH: How does this work across realms? The global object is a funny thing, as depending on where you evaluate it from, you may get different ones. If the global object is a proxy, is the system object also a proxy?","","MM: The System object is very much like the Math object","","WH: In an environment with multiple realms, there will be multiple System objects.","","DD: (draws diagram to explain WindowProxy)","","AK: Is this relevant to the System.global discussion?","","JHD: I'll reiterate that this is not adding a new capability, as you can use the Function constructor; this just gives a way to do that without eval.","","DD: Actually IE/Edge is restricted in a way that I don't understand for calling the function constructor in some ways","","MM: This is one case where it's been hard for me to contribute to the web side of the standards world","","BE: Ultimately this is about things like window.setTimeout (with a string so it will do eval)? Or what situations?","","DD: Even executing a closure.","","DD: WindowProxy is there so that, if you navigate a frame within another frame, the \"window\" object of that frame stays the same identity, so it is a \"proxy\" to an inner global object which changes on navigation. There's no way to access the inner object from within script.","","JHD: Regardless of WindowProxy, System.global returns the global object, the same one that's accessed through 'this' or whatever else.","","DH: Yes, this is the thing in the space of globalness that's relevant.","","JHD: So we need a way to access the global 'this' value, a way that's the same across all environments. The function constructor can't be called from CSP. So we have two options--the bare 'global', or System.global. I haven't found anyone do typeof global","","BF: Browserify's wrapper uses typeof global","","JHD: But actually everyone uses 'typeof process' together with that when detecting Node-ness.","","AWB: Two other options for names: Object.global","","MM: I veto that as it would violate authority separation. I want to separate authority-carrying objects from non-authority-separating objects.","","DD: But `Object.__proto__` is Function, which gives you the authority to get the global object anyway.","","MM: Function and eval are evaluators; CSP gives you the option to turn off evaluators. Any other environment such as SES/frozen realms has to intervene in the evaluators in order to constrain the scope of the evaluation. In any such environment, the function constructor has to be sanitized.","","YK: Doesn't that mean that we don't currently have authority separation, and you already have to do some work for this?","","MM: We've addressed current pain points; let's not add to the burden.","","AWB: A lot of this seems to revolve around the function constructor. Another place to hang this would be Function.global.","","MM: Let's not spend time on things that are strictly worse","","JHD: Mark has argued that this cannot be a global variable so that it's more easily secured.","","DH: Sounds like a good time to bring in the Realms API and the global scope contour, which introduce additional concepts that need work in the language. It's an open area for discussion, where we might want to expose the actual current realm.","","AK: There's something special about global. There's already three ways to access this thing; adding new ways is sorta bad. We're not adding a bunch of things; this is just accessing one thing.","","MM: Right now, none of the ways of accessing global are in the ECMAScript spec, and it's a beautiful thing that the boundary between the ES spec and the host corresponds very closely to user-mode computation and system mode computation. ES standardizes no way to cause effects on the outside world; the host provides bindings on the global object to cause effects on the outside world. Because the other things are put on the global, the global itself should be considered a host object that provides access to these things. Because there is no binding to the global object, nothing grants authority. There are several future proposals which do things like that.","","AK: We don't have any of those. Global is special. There is some advantage to making the name short. Let's say it doesn't set a convention.","","AWB: This should be a built-in module","","JHD: So far, every time this came up, we said that we don't want to block it on this; once there's a standard modules proposal, we can consider this.","","DD: We have a strong precedent for just calling this global. I want to understand your objection, Mark. It sounds like you're saying, let's not set the precedent of exposing a power object, when it's already exposed in reality in so many ways.","","MM: Because it's not in scope in the ES spec, an environment could claim conformance to ES without exposing this.","","DE: It is in the intersection of the various popular embedding environments, however.","","JHD: I went with System.global because of the nonzero compat risk of bare 'global'. However, I haven't found any concrete compat risks. The second reason is that Mark thought it would help restrict authority to put it under a namespace.","","YK: SES already has to care about this kind of thing.","","MM: We currently have a whitelist in SES. global is not one of them.","","JHD: So if you're OK with not adding a global, you don't have to do anything to SES?","","MM: I'm concerned about the maintenance cost and initialization time. Spec changes cause SES to trail, which users find painful.","","JHD: But sounds like SES users will be protected anyway","","AK: The difference between other things considered to add to System, Loader, etc and global is that they add new capabilities, whereas global does not add a new capability. It's just exposing an existing thing. Therefore it doesn't need to be added in a particular namespace, and doesn't set a precedent.","","MM: I hope that frozen realms will be added and hide the global object.","","JHD: It sounds like the requirement that it be under a namespace is not very strong, simply a preference","","MM: \"simply a preference\" is too weak. The issue of distinctions and psychological burden and precedent setting are pretty important.","","DT: You're talking about the burden on developers?","","JHD: I agree that they're real issues, but users already have the burden of having this reference.","","YK: Given that you expose the global object, seems like it doesn't give a new capability.","","MM: I'll have to think about this, but I can't approve that as a sound choice at the moment.","","JHD: If Mark were to agree to Yehuda's point, if we changed the name to 'global', would anyone object to it with the name simply 'global'?","","DD: I'd prefer 'self'","","CM: no self","","DD: Would prefer `self`","","AK: 'global' seems fine. Most people don't seem to want 'self', Domenic.","","YK, AK: This doesn't give any new capability","","JHD: Sounds like the next steps are for Mark to think through Yehuda's objection and see if he can support bare 'global', and for me to follow up with Mark, Dean and \u003cwho?\u003e","","#### Conclusion/Resolution","","- Stage 2 holds","","","","## 10.ii.b Template literal revision to stage 3","","Tim Disney","","https://tc39.es/proposal-template-literal-revision/","","Reviewers: Mark Miller and Waldemar Horwat","","TD: (recap) w/ tagged template literals, escape seq. illegal. Changes seek to allow","","- Only change: https://tc39.es/proposal-template-literal-revision/#sec-static-semantics-template-early-errors removed the parameterization of the lexical grammar productions and instead enforces early errors via static semantics attached to the syntactic grammar. This change was a result of Mark and Waldemar's review.","","TD: Approval Stage 3?","","","#### Conclusion/Resolution","","- Stage 3 acceptance","","","## 9.i.i ECMA-402 formatToParts","","Zibi Braniecki","","","ZB: Have implementation in SpiderMonkey, looking for a second implementor to proceed stage.","","DE: To help formatToParts to Stage 4, ideal to upstream to ICU","","CP: upstreaming to ICU should not be a requirement","","AK: V8 not waiting for Stage 4","","YK: The chicken-egg problem is about unflagging, not implementing.","","ZB: Hoping Chakra, JSC, or any would implement","","DD: What is the rush?","","ZB: Not a rush, but the proposal has been ready for half a year. This is the last change that remodels the API. Everything else is new editions. This change opens abilities for cleanup.","","YK: My opinion is that we've met the criteria","","AWB: Do we have two implementations?","","ZB: Yes","","AWB: Compatibility issues?","","ZB: Shipped in SM behind flag","","CP: There are a lot of new Intl features that need formatToParts","","DD: They can just be dependent","","EFT/RW: That's bogus.","","AWB: There is experience from significant usage? Want to hear about that","","ZB: Used in consumer-facing product, Panasonic TVs running FirefoxOS.
